In this installment we follow Sybella's story. She has a few secrets, one being- that she is D'lbrets daughter. As a handmaiden of death, she is left with the task of returning to her fathers home to act as a spy. There are so many dark memories of things that await her there. <br><br>I wasn't sure how I would like this one since it didn't follow Ismae and Duval- but I am glad I gave it a chance. It only took a minute to get wrapped up in Sybellas story. She has a horrific past. It was a little harder to read than the first. There are some disturbing things that take place and by no means, does she have a pretty story. <br><br>Enter Beast- not easy on the eyes, and the name Beast may fit his body, but not his personality. It wasn't hard to fall for Beast and his big heart. The writing was once again beautiful, and pacing flowed nicely. <br><br>I really enjoyed Sybellas whole personality a little more than I did Ismaes from Grave Mercy. She wasn't as soft and I liked that. But I do have to admit- I liked Grave Mercy a little more than Dark Triumph. I think maybe since it was the first in the series, but this was still a great follow up to GM! I'm looking forward to the last book, Mortal Heart, so that I can get all caught up for the new series Courting Darkness!</span>

<div id="review_583246612" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/583246612" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/583246612?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer583246612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10397225986993429424">Rating: 3.5 Stars<br/><br/>Where <i>Grave Mercy</i> was a lie, a novel about dancing and political parties deftly wrapped up with a bow-tie of kick-ass assassin-nuns that never assassinated, <i>Dark Triumph</i> is more of the dark, bad-ass story I was looking for with LaFevers's debut last year. Nevertheless, while <i>Grave Mercy</i> was a sore disappointment, I am glad to admit that <i>Dark Triumph</i> completely won me over. It seems to be the case this year that series I swore off of last year have come back to haunt me, making m</span>
  <span id="freeText10397225986993429424" style="display:none">Rating: 3.5 Stars<br /><br />Where <i>Grave Mercy</i> was a lie, a novel about dancing and political parties deftly wrapped up with a bow-tie of kick-ass assassin-nuns that never assassinated, <i>Dark Triumph</i> is more of the dark, bad-ass story I was looking for with LaFevers's debut last year. Nevertheless, while <i>Grave Mercy</i> was a sore disappointment, I am glad to admit that <i>Dark Triumph</i> completely won me over. It seems to be the case this year that series I swore off of last year have come back to haunt me, making me eat my words with my utter love for their companion novels. It happened with <i>Scarlet</i> and it has happened again with <i>Dark Triumph,</i> so to any other companion novels out there? Come at me! ;) <br /><br /><i>Dark Triumph</i> takes place in the same historic setting <i>Grave Mercy</i> was placed and the writing isn't significantly different either. Instead, what makes this novel so much better than its predecessor is that <b>it is actually about assassin-nuns.</b> Sybella is an experienced killer, but also the daughter of the evil Lord d'Albert, sent back to his home with the promise of extracting revenge upon him. Once within the castle, however, Sybella is thrown sharply back to her dark life, watching as friends are slaughtered ruthlessly by her father and forced to give into the wishes of her half-brother Julian who has become a lover instead of the childhood protector he once was. When Sybella receives orders to free a prisoner in the dungeons, the revered Beast, she resolves to exact her revenge on her father at last, all while freeing his most valued prisoner. Life, it seems, has slightly different plans for Sybella...<br /><br />What makes <i>Dark Triumph</i> such a success for me is Sybella. Although the layers behind Sybella's dark past are artfully revealed as the novel progresses, it is evident from the beginning itself that she has lived a brutal life. As a woman, there is little use for her in her father's household and despite successfully dispatching of his allies, she longs to put an end to the man who has made her life a living hell. Yet, through these conditions, she perseveres. While her faith in Mortmain wavers at times, her courage and strength never does, making her an inspiring character in the way that naive, dancing Ismae never was. Furthermore, Sybella doesn't fear death or murder. What she fears is the spreading evil of her own family and her cursed existence as a d'Albert herself, but all this only makes her a far more full-fledged and hurting character than we imagine. As the full story of Sybella's past comes to light, it is only with awe that we can chart how far she has come, even from the beginning of the novel. <br /><br />Along with Sybella, though, the slow burning romance she shares with Beast is one to behold. Both Sybella and Beast share a love for killing, but they retain their humanity in a way d'Albert fails to. What makes their bond so strong, though, is the fact that Beast sees Sybella for who she is and never tries to stifle her. While the other men in Sybella's life mold her into what they want, Beast accepts Sybella as she is with her assassin skills, dark past, and treachery. Granted, he yearns to protect her, but he also knows that Sybella is more than capable of protecting herself - and he lets her. Although Beast has a large, scary, scarred, and ugly appearance, he is a complete softie inside and lacks the alpha male tendencies that make me roll my eyes. All in all, it's safe to say I've fallen for him - quite hard. <br /><br />What prevents me from giving <i>Dark Triumph</i> a higher rating, however, is the fact that a solid eighty pages could be cut off from the beginning. Folks, it takes a <i>long</i> time to get the ball rolling on this plot line and it is wholly unnecessary. While it does shed much light on Sybella's past, I feel as if the same effect could have been achieved with a fewer number of pages. Additionally, <i>Dark Triumph</i> is one of those rare instances where I recognize that, technically, a book contains no flaws but a slight lack of connection with it yields to a lesser enjoyment of the book. I'm not entirely sure <i>why</i> I didn't enjoy the novel as much as I hoped, mostly because I <i>liked</i> it, but my enjoyment of it hovered on just <i>mere</i> like opposed to <i>really</i> enjoyed. Not sure why. I suspect it may be because of the first few chapters or even because the political scheme which was more war-related - which I really liked, mind you, but which did take away limelight from the characters on more than one occasion. Even the writing, at times, could be a bit off-putting in certain scenes, so all together, I did not wholly <i>love</i> this book. <br /><br />Nevertheless, <i>Dark Triumph</i> is, as far as I'm concerned, a triumph when it comes to a solid sequel and I find myself eagerly looking forward to Annith's story next. If I'd found myself saying that last year, I would have been sorely surprised, but at this point, I am ready for more pleasant surprises to come my way. <br /><br />You can read <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2013/04/review-dark-triumph-by-rl-lafevers.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="10397225986993429424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2646590422" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2646590422" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8575414-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441431450p2/8575414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2646590422?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/8575414-emma">Emma</a>

        rated it

<div id="review_1073332169" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1073332169" />
    <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books"><img alt="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415550632p2/5892196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1073332169?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books">Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1073332169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9094516975654608935">This review can also be found at <a href='http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carole's Random Life</a><br/><br/><i>I received an advance reader edition of this book from Houghton Mifflin Harcourt via Net Galley for the purpose of providing an honest review.</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382809015ra/6217526.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>5 Stars!<br/><br/>I loved the first book in this series and to be honest I really didn't think the second one would be able to top it. But it did. This book was absolutely amazing. This was the kind of book that I hated to put down. This story grabbed me and made me feel for the characters. This type of novel is e</span>
  <span id="freeText9094516975654608935" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole's Random Life</a><br><br><i>I received an advance reader edition of this book from Houghton Mifflin Harcourt via Net Galley for the purpose of providing an honest review.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382809015ra/6217526.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>5 Stars!<br><br>I loved the first book in this series and to be honest I really didn't think the second one would be able to top it. But it did. This book was absolutely amazing. This was the kind of book that I hated to put down. This story grabbed me and made me feel for the characters. This type of novel is exactly why I read. I read to be swept away by a story, to feel for the characters, and hope for their triumph. <br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>We all have our secrets. And our scars.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>This book picks up right where Grave Mercy left off. Sybella has been placed in the home of d'Albret, who is by all accounts an evil man. This book had a darker feel that the prior book in the series. It also had a lot more action. Sybella is given the task of rescuing the man being kept in d'Albret's dungeon. That man is known as Beast and is known and loved throughout the region.<br><br>After fleeing the dungeon with Beast and his former guard, Sybella works to keep Beast alive. We quickly learn that these two people have a lot in common. They have both killed and are good at it. They both have a horrible past that they have been forced to overcome. They are both also very stubborn and determined to succeed. <br><br>The writing in this book was absolutely remarkable. I really did not care of Sybella too much in the first book but by the end of this book my heart was breaking for her. She was tough and a survivor and one of the most wonderful characters I have read. Beast was very likeable in the first book and as we learned more about him in this story that feeling only grew. Beast was able to see Sybella for who she really was and look beyond her past. These two characters made the story and I found myself hoping that they would find strength and healing in each other.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Through the darkness, his big warm hand tenderly takes hold of mine, and I want to weep at the understanding of his touch.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>I would highly recommend this book to really just about everyone. This is the second book by Robin LaFevers that I have had a chance to read and I will definitely be reading more. I would recommend that this trilogy be read in order as it is a continuation of the overall story. I cannot wait for the final book in this trilogy to be released and I hope that we see more of Sybella and Beast in that novel. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9094516975654608935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1258344-cinda?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer580256491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16232572952484990289">It seems impossible, but this one is even better than Grave Mercy. Great characters, great story, high stakes, and elements of history, mystery and magic. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2277045-gail-carriger?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2277045-gail-carriger?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2277045-gail-carriger?shelf=ya">ya</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1092210459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1866972159823099432">On the flip side from Ismae, Sybella's journey is about closure. This second book Dark Triumph is a much tougher read, and darker than I normally prefer. Sybella, terribly abused and broken, is sent back from the only sanctuary she has ever known into the vipers nest that is the family that nearly destroyed her sanity. Unlike Ismae, she knows she can't trust anyone, ever. Her journey is one of rising above this background and becoming the person she should have been all along, had she not suffer</span>
  <span id="freeText1866972159823099432" style="display:none">On the flip side from Ismae, Sybella's journey is about closure. This second book Dark Triumph is a much tougher read, and darker than I normally prefer. Sybella, terribly abused and broken, is sent back from the only sanctuary she has ever known into the vipers nest that is the family that nearly destroyed her sanity. Unlike Ismae, she knows she can't trust anyone, ever. Her journey is one of rising above this background and becoming the person she should have been all along, had she not suffered such an abusive childhood.<br /><br />I tend to prefer my books on the lighter end of the spectrum, so I did find this one hard to read. However, once Sybella escapes (no spoiler there, you know it has to happen) and is out of the oppressive family fold and the romance thread begins, I liked her that much more because of her darkness. Sybella could have been a very unlikeable character, particularly as she is paired with one of the most likeable side characters from the previous book, but the romance and her personality evolution is handled deftly enough to make it plausible. My advise is just to read and don't stop to think about what that kind of abuse would actually do to a girl. I should say it's never graphic, which is how I came to stomach it.<br /><br />I would understand, however, struggling with this book after the first. They are quite different characters and stories.<br /><br />FROM THE GRAVE MERCY REVIEW:<br /><br />There series premise: three girls from difference backgrounds are deemed daughters of death and taken in to a mysterious convent where they are trained as assassins, called death's handmaidens. Each is then sent from the convent into the politics of late 1400s Brittany where they find self confidence through love, purpose, and place in society.<br /><br />The writing: rich period color, first person perspective, strong voice, some graphic violence, modest sex scenes, excellent heroic counterparts, complex politics. Close accepting friendship between girls and women, betrayal by adult role models.</span>

<div id="review_552057492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/552057492" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/552057492?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer552057492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3545795697054722105">Now we're talking! <br/>This is what an assassin's story looks like :D<br/><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/r-l-lafevers/review-dark-triumph.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407169239i/10649876.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Less political compared to GRAVE MERCY, but just as captivating, DARK TRIUMPH takes its readers on a ride full of adventure and suspense, of deception and lies. And not only is it filled with action and assassin missions and strategies, but we also get a few glimpses into the lives of some of our beloved characters from the first book. There is a bit of mystery that keeps the reader going through the story but what really won m</span>
  <span id="freeText3545795697054722105" style="display:none">Now we're talking! <br>This is what an assassin's story looks like :D<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/r-l-lafevers/review-dark-triumph.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407169239i/10649876.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Less political compared to GRAVE MERCY, but just as captivating, DARK TRIUMPH takes its readers on a ride full of adventure and suspense, of deception and lies. And not only is it filled with action and assassin missions and strategies, but we also get a few glimpses into the lives of some of our beloved characters from the first book. There is a bit of mystery that keeps the reader going through the story but what really won me over were the killing skills and the strong wold building – and I actually like it when authors take liberties in order to make the story more intriguing, more action driven, with all the details accounted for in the end.<br><br>As many people have mentioned before, this story feels a lot more personal because of the nature of Sybella’s mission. Driven to the border of madness by unimaginable horrors endured at home, Sybella finds refugee on the monastery and for a while she finally feels at peace. She is trained in the deadly arts and she becomes really good at it, as not only does she lack hesitation towards killing when ordered, but she actually enjoys it as it gives her plenty of control. She becomes a master at hiding her fears, she is dangerous with most weapons, especially knives, and the one thing that keeps her going is her need for vengeance, her longing to put an end to the man who has made her life a living hell – her father (an absolutely disgusting character, a true monster, one of the worst villains out there).<br><br>But deep down she is a tortured, broken girl full of anger and despair, searching in vain for the saint’s guidance. Despite her strong spirit and her ability to kill without effort, she is still haunted by her brutal, tragic past. So when she is sent back to her damaged family (with D’Albret – the monstrous father, and also Julian – the incestuous, messed-up brother) all she relies on is the promise that she will get her revenge - but that exact order never comes; and instead of delivering his death, as promised, she receives other orders and she is even instructed to set free a prisoner from the dungeons.<br><br>With her patience running low, Sybella drags out of prison a mortally wounded knight, and somehow she find herself kidnaped by him in return. After this, everything starts to spin out of control, her faith starts to shake even more and step by step she gets to make her own choices about who lives and dies. And because the story wouldn’t be complete without a bit of romance, Beast and Sybella find out that they have many things in common and that they complete each other – in fact it feels like they’ve been broken into imperfect pieces that fit perfectly together. [...]<br><br>I will leave you to discover what the story is about, but there are some other characters that I should mention: like Ismae and Duval – I loved to see them again. Also there is the brother, Julian whose mind was just as twisted by the monstrosity of a father that he had, if not quite a lot more. Not all the things he did can be justified, but he did redeemed himself just a tiny,tiny bit by the ending.<br><br>All in one, DARK TRIUMPH was an absolute delight. I loved this story and I can’t wait to read the next book in the series, which I assume that will be just as great.<br><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/r-l-lafevers/review-dark-triumph.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334106i/693595.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>*Find the complete review at: <a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/r-l-lafevers/review-dark-triumph.html" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>

<div id="review_668285676" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/668285676" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22195799-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514812938p2/22195799.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/668285676?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/22195799-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781328567666" href="/book/show/38640726-dark-triumph">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22195799-michelle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer668285676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9002531160987090712">I never really appreciated this story and Sybella like I do now. When I read this in 2016, this was actually my least favorite of the three books. I’m not even sure why. It just was even when I loved all of the books so much. Sybella is such a complex characters with an incredibly difficult life. She is filled with darkness and not much light around her. She has only a few people left in the world she loves, like her sisters and her blood sisters as well later in her life. I really admire her st</span>
  <span id="freeText9002531160987090712" style="display:none">I never really appreciated this story and Sybella like I do now. When I read this in 2016, this was actually my least favorite of the three books. I’m not even sure why. It just was even when I loved all of the books so much. Sybella is such a complex characters with an incredibly difficult life. She is filled with darkness and not much light around her. She has only a few people left in the world she loves, like her sisters and her blood sisters as well later in her life. I really admire her strength, her desire to protect the ones she loves and her determination. Also Beast as her friend, lover and as the person that sees her how she really is and not how she would like people to see her as. She isn’t unfeeling and bloodthirsty (we’ll only sometimes). She has a heart but doesn’t want to show it as there are far too many around her to use that against her. There is just so much more to her than people think. So many secrets she wants to lock away and I’m so glad she found those whom she can trust to watch her back. Ones that she can finally open up to without worries of judgement and abandonment. This story is filled unexpectedly with so much love and I’m so glad Sybella found some reasons to smile again. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br />*Edit: 1/8/16<br /><br />(Re-read review) I will try to make this a spoiler free review. <br /><br />I love the first book in this trilogy, <i>Grave Mercy</i> because of the characters and how the history was woven into a story about nun assassins (which is always awesome to read about). In this sequel, we get to know the disturbed and broken, Sybella as she is sent back to the household of Count d'Albret as a spy for the Duchess and to kill D'Albret when the time arrives. A message arrives from the Abbess to rescue the captured knight, Beast of Waroch, before D'Albret can use him to exact his own evil plans. When Sybella accidently escorts Beast to the Duchess, she finds a friend and companion in him. They find a past connection between them and thus brings horrific past events to the present which only add to Sybella's tragic story. Sybella's story is less political and much more personal but there is still plenty of action, romance, and danger. <br /><br />If you thought you hated D'Albret in the first book, well, surprise, you will want to send him personally straight to hell after reading this one. Somehow, even with all of her scars, both physical and mental, Sybella still manages to be a badass, protect others, survive, and find love. You really have to give props to her for making it work in the end. We get more of Ismae, Duval, and Beast so we all win in this part. Beast and Sybella are absolutely perfect for each other. They have opposite personalities, but once the fight is one, they are one in the same. <br /><br />This one is much darker than the first not necessarily better or worse, just different. I had way to much enjoyment when she had the chance to kill someone. However, they were usually traitors or trying to hurt someone so I shouldn't feel that bad. Another great read. I will be heading over to Annith's story in <i>Mortal Heart</i> very soon. I seriously love this trilogy. <br /><br />"I have my whole life before me, and for the first time, it is filled not with fear and darkness, but with love and promise."<br /><br />Overall: 5 stars<br />Recommendation: Oh yeah!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9002531160987090712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286805202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11457727780465397737">A copy of Dark Triumph was provided to me by Houghton Mifflin Books for Children for review purposes.<br/><br/><i>​'The abbess and I had a different sort of relationship. One built on mutual dislike and distrust, brought together only by our shared needs: mine for a sanctuary, hers for a finely honed weapon she could let loose as Mortain willed. I trust her as much as I do a viper.'​</i><br/><br/>It seems as if each hand maiden of death ha​s​ her own story to tell and in Dark Triumph we ​get to experience Lady Sybella's. </span>
  <span id="freeText11457727780465397737" style="display:none">A copy of Dark Triumph was provided to me by Houghton Mifflin Books for Children for review purposes.<br><br><i>​'The abbess and I had a different sort of relationship. One built on mutual dislike and distrust, brought together only by our shared needs: mine for a sanctuary, hers for a finely honed weapon she could let loose as Mortain willed. I trust her as much as I do a viper.'​</i><br><br>It seems as if each hand maiden of death ha​s​ her own story to tell and in Dark Triumph we ​get to experience Lady Sybella's. And hers is quite grim and ​desolate.​ Sybella manages to escape from the frightening place she was forced to call home for most of her life and finds herself at the convent; a place where she finally feels at peace. <br><br><i>'As Death's handmaiden, I must be in place so I may strike when the time comes.'</i><br><br>Her peace is short-lived, however, as the abbess instructs her that Mortain wishes her to return to her father so that she can be in a prime position in d'Albret's household to gain priceless information in order to aid the abbess. The horrors she endured in that household does not make it an easy order to accept.<br><br>Sybella is much more 'rough around the edges' in comparison to Ismae but her story was still just as riveting. Much of the story is spent with Sybella ​trying to come to terms with her upbringing and clinging desperately to the fact that d'Albert is not her true father and that she is nothing like him. <br><br><i>​​​​​'Do I enjoy killing? Is it the act itself that brings me joy? Or do I embrace the sense of higher purpose it gives me?'</i><br><br>At its center, Dark Triumph is a story of faith and belief. Faith and belief that Sybella is nothing like her loathsome father and that Mortain is her true father. Faith and belief that the men she has killed that did not bear a marque still deserved their deaths and that it isn't a sin against Mortain. She struggles consistently with these thoughts and it sets the tone for the entire story.<br><br>​​​Much like Grave Mercy, Dark Triumph does include a romance but it's perfectly balanced so as to not overpower the story in any way. The Beast of Waroch: the perfectly imperfect love interest is the perfect love interest for Sybella. He's the one that could ever come closest to being able to truly understand her and loving her for who she undoubtedly is. <br><br>​Agonizingly heartbreaking, Sybella has lived through so much pain and misery in such a short time. It may be easy to commiserate with her, however, it's even easier to praise her for her strength and ability to endure. Sybella is a true survivor, an inspiration, and an unbelievably strong character that you won't likely forget.<br><br>*All quotes taken are from an uncorrected proof*<br><br><div>
  <a href="http://sweet-tidbits.blogspot.com/" title="Sweet Tidbits" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380351064i/704765.gif" alt="Sweet Tidbits" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fTU3akRcyuN8SXA8jJKxxZMHx7C3MXjy8kOQuG/+kd8kBvRKIs4ScaV4Xb/Cr+jYlKJEFRhOXzUnzyvpXICxIQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HXxOtMkTRvu0WOB8ugBMNZ/0aCcMfDjF0Ec1FcukbE9ET42Ur4GeaW1pzf/0PRUomFHrgqMDHwIFy45E+NpMsQ==')})
  }
//]]>
